#MMIW A beautiful profile of a Native Woman! A beautiful profile of a Native Woman with a Sacred Circle of Glow! The Sacred Circle of Glow could denote the cycle of life for a woman as a life-giver, the legacy carrier, the center of our world, and the sacred healer. The white light around this beautiful profile of a Native Woman announces that the Creator loves her. However, this white light also represents this spirit is a Legacy of Violence which started before 1492 and continues today. As the ribbons encircle the beautiful Native Woman’s skirt, we think of slavery, stolen, sold, abused, murdered, raped, genocidal attempts-legally and illegally, to today’s messed up jurisdictional boundaries, the racist attitude of “don’t want to bother with an Indian”, emergency services not available for the victims, and no database for such a statistically insignificant population. Let’s include our little girls and boys in this Legacy of Violence that has lost their matrilineal tie to their culture education to their identity. Lines of Action: Support the numerous native #MMIW organizations and coalitions, support native youth, support creation of a National Day of Awareness for Murdered and Missing Native Women and Girls. It was never our way to harm HER mentally or physically. We were always taught to treat our women with respect and understanding. 1269 Record Crossing Road, Suite E, Dallas, TX 75235, 214-941-1050, X275. You are invited to come and meet the Director Anna Duy and Assistant Director Anthony Nauni. In order to provide assistance to enrolled Comanche tribal members residing in the Dallas metroplex and surrounding areas, the Comanche Nation voted to establish a satellite office in 2013. There are over 1400 Comanche Nation tribal members residing throughout the state of Texas. Tribal Members can be assisted with information and application with various services offered by the Comanche Nation, such as upcoming and current events, Social Services (Emergency Assistance and Bereavement), Enrollment, Diabetes Program, Student Services, Workforce, Higher Education, Optometry Program, and Prescription Assistance. The Texas Comanche Nation tribal members population continues to grow every day and The Dallas Outreach Office looks forward to the future of the Comanche Nation. Comanche tribal members, we invite you and encourage you to support the 6th annual American Indian Heritage Day’s tribal recognition of the Comanche Nation on September 29, 2018, at the Lone Star Park, 1000 Lone Star Parkway, Grand Prairie, Texas, 10 a.m. – 3 p.m. Anthony Nauni Comanche Nation Dallas Outreach Office Comanche National Museum and Cultural Center Johnny Tiddark Anna Wang Duy through Film\" announces the 3rd Annual Film Festival Sept 5 - Sept 10, 2018. \nFor more Information: Contact Ratee Apana, executive Director at 513 886 5817. iffcincy@gmail.com\n​\nCincinnati, July 15, 2018.  The Indian Film Festival of Cincinnati (IFFC) announced their third year of celebrating independent, diaspora films from/about/connected to the Indian subcontinent. This prestigious film festival is the only Indian Film festival in Ohio. The festival is organized by the India Cincinnati Sister City and will showcase 10 award winning Feature Films and 24 short films and host a red carpet gala!\n \nThis year's festival will include a soft opening with a tribute to veteran actor Shashi Kapoor of the Indian Cinema and a tribute to director, James Ivory at the Cincinnati Art Museum on Wednesday Sept 5, 6Pm Cocktails, followed by film at 6:45PM.\nThe opening film will be screened at the Main Street Theater, University of Cincinnati on Sept 7. Event starts at 6PM, Film starts at 7PM. followed by a gala at 9PM at the Tangeman Main Hall at the University of Cincinnati. \n \n34 films have been selected from the 467 submissions received this year and will be screened at the Freedom Center,  Esquire theatre, Mariemont Theatre, Kenwood Theatre, Cincinnati Art Museum and the Main Street Theater. After parties will be held at Ludlow area restaurants and at the quarter Bistro in Mariemont. The festival will include industry panels on Thursday and Friday 9:30-12PM at the Main Street Theater, University of Cincinnati.  All films are subtitled in English. The festival’s film lineup include premiers of several international award winning films. We are thrilled to be able to share these films with the Cincinnati audience.   Many of the films are made in the US. The films will cover a range of important issues such as transgender, LGBTQ, immigration, racism, elderly children and parent relationships, young sibling relationships, etc.\n​\nIndividual tickets can be purchased on the Festival site www.iffcincy.com or at the respective venues or their web sites. Tickets will go on sale August 15. Gala Tickets are available on www.iffcincy.com. \nWe invite you to experience five fun filled days of independent cinema from the Indian and South Asian diaspora across the globe!\nOur Schedule.\n​\nOur Mission: To engage diversity through Film. To bring understanding and reflection to the common human values that bind us both because of and in spite of our diversity. \nOur Cause: Net proceeds of ticket sales will go towards need based scholarships for Cincinnati Public High School for the Cincinnati Sister Cities Youth Ambassador Program (India). Students learn about the culture history, diversity and economy of India through classes and travel. Students are then paired with local corporate mentors and University students as a first step towards making University education their goal.\n​\n \n \nSCHEDULE OF EVENTS AND VENUES\nINDIAN FILM FESTIVAL OF CINCINNATI, SEPT 5-10, 2018\n \nSeptember 5, Wednesday 6:30PM, Venue: Cincinnati Art Museum\nMovie:\" HEAT & DUST\" Tribute to Shashi Kapoor, cocktails, learn about the upcoming films watch trailers or listen to directors\n \nSeptember 6, Thursday\n-          9:30 AM -12 PM, 2PM-4PM, Venue: UC Main Street Theater, Tangeman Center UC\nEvent: Industry talks.
